  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer13068990279689764644"><b>The Barnes & Noble Review</b><br/>With the debut of his first young-adult novel, science fiction writer Terry Pratchett invites readers ages 12 and up to visit Discworld -- an imaginary land well known to Pratchett's adult following. At the heart of this tale is a slightly twisted take on the old Pied Piper theme, a talking, thinking cat named Maurice, and a supporting cast of equa</span>
  <span id="freeText13068990279689764644" style="display:none"><b>The Barnes &amp; Noble Review</b><br />With the debut of his first young-adult novel, science fiction writer Terry Pratchett invites readers ages 12 and up to visit Discworld -- an imaginary land well known to Pratchett's adult following. At the heart of this tale is a slightly twisted take on the old Pied Piper theme, a talking, thinking cat named Maurice, and a supporting cast of equally talented rats who bear such comical names as Big Savings, Nourishing, and Dangerous Beans. <br /><p><br />Maurice and the rats have teamed up with a young lad named Keith to implement a clever moneymaking scheme. Upon entering a town, the rats make a general nuisance of themselves -- stealing food and widdling on things -- until the townsfolk become desperate to get rid of them. Then Maurice and Keith appear on the scene and offer to save the day by ridding the town of its infestation for a small fee. It seems like a surefire plan until the group arrives in the town of Bad Blintz and gets hooked up with Malicia, a young girl with a vivid imagination and a knack for finding trouble. When it's discovered that Bad Blintz already has a rat problem -- one that a couple of shifty-eyed rat catchers claim to have under control -- things turn deadly. For lurking beneath the town's streets is an obstacle course of mangling rattraps and noxious poisons. And beyond that is a monster so powerful and ugly, even Malicia couldn't imagine it. <br /></p><p><br />As Maurice and the rats battle for their very survival, a number of provocative themes surface: life after death, good versus evil, and the sacrifice of the few for the many. But be forewarned -- those in search of lighter fare in these troubled times may not find what they are looking for in Pratchett's vision Despite plenty of razor-sharp wit and lighthearted moments, this tale has an underbelly as dark as the tunnels beneath Bad Blintz. Though <i>The Amazing Maurice and His Educated Rodents</i> is deeply witty and engaging, some readers may find parts of the story -- descriptions of how some of the rats die and how others eat their dead -- rather intense. <i>(Beth Amos)</i></p></span>
  <a data-text-id="13068990279689764644" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1960056346" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1960056346" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1960056346?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552546935" href="/book/show/1191652.The_Amazing_Maurice_His_Educated_Rodents">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1960056346" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12239709614520340761">For children?<br/><br/>Maybe, but there are some dark issues going on and dealt with from the master himself.<br/><br/>Terry Pratchett’s first Discworld “story” designating it as written for children (followed by the wonderful Tiffany Aching sub-series) but I would submit this is YA territory, no warm fuzzy Disney moments here.<br/><br/>First of all, if there was a film this reminded me of it would be the 1995 Chris Noonan film Babe. In this very good movie, a young piglet confronts the contrast and distinction of animals as</span>
  <span id="freeText12239709614520340761" style="display:none">For children?<br><br>Maybe, but there are some dark issues going on and dealt with from the master himself.<br><br>Terry Pratchett’s first Discworld “story” designating it as written for children (followed by the wonderful Tiffany Aching sub-series) but I would submit this is YA territory, no warm fuzzy Disney moments here.<br><br>First of all, if there was a film this reminded me of it would be the 1995 Chris Noonan film Babe. In this very good movie, a young piglet confronts the contrast and distinction of animals as pets and being loved as a part of the family while also being food.<br><br>“That’ll do pig, that’ll do.”<br><br>Here, Pratchett has crafted a clever parody of the Pied Piper of Hamelin story, with of course, some Discworld twists, turns, what haves you (not the Brothers Grimm but rather the Sisters Grimm). Channeling Orwell in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7613.Animal_Farm" title="Animal Farm by George Orwell" rel="nofollow noopener">Animal Farm</a> and Daniel Keyes <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18373.Flowers_for_Algernon" title="Flowers for Algernon by Daniel Keyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Flowers for Algernon</a>, Pratchett has again returned to the ubiquitous phenomena of animals becoming sentient after living and eating in and around Unseen University. Seems the residual magic boosts the critter’s intelligence and provides a fecundity of fictional MAGIC for all us Discworld aficionados out here. Maurice the cat and his band of smart RATS have teamed up with Keith the teenage piper to swindle some Uberwald villages.<br><br>As in all of Pratchett’s books, though, there is a lot going on besides talking rats and some dubiously naïve villagers. This is also one of his darker outings, which again makes me wonder about this being marketed to wee ones, unless Pratchett in his INFINITE AND IMPRESSIVE GENIUS makes that point, it is the young ones who can still get the irony of sentient rats pretending to be led away by a fake flutist. <br><br>Recommended, one the best Discworld books.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1547816502i/26936141._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="237" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="12239709614520340761" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1960056346">

<div id="review_14801337" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/14801337" />
    <a title="Dan Schwent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent"><img alt="Dan Schwent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593973948p2/870755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/14801337?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan Schwent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan Schwent" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent">Dan Schwent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060012335" href="/book/show/64223.The_Amazing_Maurice_and_His_Educated_Rodents">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=young-adultery">young-adultery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=pratchett">pratchett</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2010">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer14801337" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6619304769257309955">Maurice, a talking cat, leads a group of talking mice and a stupid-looking kid into a town called Bad Blintz looking for one last score with their pied piper scam. Only Bad Blintz has troubles of its own...<br/><br/>Terry Pratchett really knows how to write a kids book. I would have devoured this thing when I was a lad. Maurice and the rats are good characters, as is Keith, the aforementioned stupid-looking kid. The origin of Maurice and the rats' intelligence was fairly well done. Hell, it's a fantasy st</span>
  <span id="freeText6619304769257309955" style="display:none">Maurice, a talking cat, leads a group of talking mice and a stupid-looking kid into a town called Bad Blintz looking for one last score with their pied piper scam. Only Bad Blintz has troubles of its own...<br /><br />Terry Pratchett really knows how to write a kids book. I would have devoured this thing when I was a lad. Maurice and the rats are good characters, as is Keith, the aforementioned stupid-looking kid. The origin of Maurice and the rats' intelligence was fairly well done. Hell, it's a fantasy story. How much explanation do you need? Pratchett took the classic story of the pied piper and Discworld-ed it up with questions of philosophy, destiny, and leadership. And rat-kings.<br /><br />Why only a three? The rat king bit felt tacked on at the last minute, although I enjoy me a good rat-king. While the humor was good, I didn't feel it was as good as the adult Discworld novels, subtle sex jokes excluded. Being a Discworld novel, things didn't quite end up all hunky-dory at the end but it was still a good ending.<br /><br />Pratchett crafted a good young adult novel here. If you have some YA's in your house, go ahead and nab this one for them.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6619304769257309955" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16358200710515719796" style="display:none"><b>"The important thing about adventures, thought Mr Bunnsy, was that they shouldn't be so long as to make you miss mealtimes."</b><br /><br /><b>"I suppose there is a Big Cat in the Sky, isn't there?"<br />"I'M SURPRISED AT YOU, MAURICE. <span id="freeTextContainer5377546604903356024"><br/>Re-Read this recently while traveling. It's interesting to see Pratchett's first run at writing something officially YA. <br/><br/>It's a good read. Smart. Funny. And pleasantly stand-alone. It's easy to see why he won the Carnegie award for it. <br/><br/>But in my opinion, it doesn't hold a candle to his later YA books that feature Tiffany Aching: Wee Free Men, Hat Full of Sky, etc. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34494.The_Wee_Free_Men__Discworld___30_' title='The Wee Free Men (Discworld, #30) by Terry Pratchett' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Wee Free Men</a><br/><br/>pat<br/></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/349494756" />
    <a title="Clouds" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9374686-clouds"><img alt="Clouds" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514641128p2/9374686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/349494756?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clouds" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clouds" href="/user/show/9374686-clouds">Clouds</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552546935" href="/book/show/1191652.The_Amazing_Maurice_His_Educated_Rodents">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=pub-2000s">pub-2000s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=discworld">discworld</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer349494756" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10085945630662013485"><a href='http://www.theaceofclouds.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380317319i/689370.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>Following the resounding success of my <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/332414-reading-lists?chapter=2' rel='nofollow noopener'>Locus Quest</a>, I faced a dilemma: which reading list to follow it up with? Variety is the spice of life, so I’ve decided to diversify and pursue six different lists simultaneously. This book falls into my <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/332414-reading-lists?chapter=8' rel='nofollow noopener'>FINISHING THE SERIES!</a> list.<br/><br/>I loves me a good series! But I'm terrible for starting a new series before finishing my last - so this reading list is all about trying to close out those series I've got on the go.</b><br/><br/>I remember being given a copy of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34517.Reaper_Man' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <i>Reaper Ma</i></a></span>
  <span id="freeText10085945630662013485" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.theaceofclouds.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380317319i/689370.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>Following the resounding success of my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/332414-reading-lists?chapter=2" rel="nofollow noopener">Locus Quest</a>, I faced a dilemma: which reading list to follow it up with? Variety is the spice of life, so I’ve decided to diversify and pursue six different lists simultaneously. This book falls into my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/332414-reading-lists?chapter=8" rel="nofollow noopener">FINISHING THE SERIES!</a> list.<br><br>I loves me a good series! But I'm terrible for starting a new series before finishing my last - so this reading list is all about trying to close out those series I've got on the go.</b><br><br>I remember being given a copy of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34517.Reaper_Man" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Reaper Man</i>
</a> when I was a wee boy. When Death took on the prototype mechanical harvester, my first major author-crush began and it's never let-up.<br><br>In my teenage years I re-read my favourite <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40650-discworld" rel="nofollow noopener">Discworld</a> books so many times that their spines cracked and pages fell out. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Sir Terry</a> will always be an idol, an icon and a source of inspiration.<br><br>But somehow this one passed me by. I think it's because it's a stand-alone within the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40650-discworld" rel="nofollow noopener">Discworld</a> universe, and those have never been my favourites. Also, I'm not yet sold on the young-adult <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40650-discworld" rel="nofollow noopener">Discworld</a> books. Before <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/64333.The_Amazing_Maurice_and_His_Educated_Rodents_Discworld_28_" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>
    <b>The Amazing Maurice</b>
  </i>
</a> I'd only read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34494.The_Wee_Free_Men" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>The Wee Free Men</i>
</a> and I wasn't convinced, so I felt little urgency to grab a copy.<br><br>This is a good book! <br><br>It's a great concept (talking cat, rats and sidekick human boy scamming villages as a rat plague and the Piper). <br>It's funny. <br>It's got great dark touches for a y-a book. <br>It explores corners of the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40650-discworld" rel="nofollow noopener">Discworld</a> map that hadn't been fully tapped. <br>Maurice is a great character. <br>Dangerous Beans is an amazing name! <br>The Mr Bunsy satire element is done superbly.<br><br>As a huge <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Pratchett</a> fan, I would read his descriptions of paint drying. This - this goes down like cold lemonade on a hot summer day. I devoured this book like it was covered in Nutella.<br><br>So why only three stars?<br><br>(This is almost an exact parrot of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/14801337" rel="nofollow noopener">Dan's review</a>)<br> - but the rat-king felt tacked on at the end. Great scenes for sure, but the story felt more episodic than cohesive.<br> - Keith, (Maurice's pet human) just never got more that a 'meh' from me, my heart was all with the rats come the end.<br> - had I read it back when I was young, we might have gelled better, but as it was I felt like I was standing outside the story-circle, imagining how a youngster would enjoy it, rather than being truly gripped myself.<br><br>I've only got a couple more <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40650-discworld" rel="nofollow noopener">Discworld</a> books I've not read, both part of the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/96852-discworld---tiffany-aching" rel="nofollow noopener">Tiffany Aching</a> y-a series. And then I will (after many years of negligence) be 100% up-to-date with the series! <br><br><b>After this I read: </b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/332063936" rel="nofollow noopener">Jitterbug Perfume</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10085945630662013485" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1065399849" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1065399849?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/28163422-the-amazing-maurice-and-his-educated-rodents">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1065399849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer731929832568852">This was one of the first <i>Discworld</i> novels I've ever read, the German translation back then though. I'm very pleased to report that the reading experience was even better this time - partly because the original is always better, partly because I now understood certain side-stabs and references, which was very rewarding.<br/><br/>It's part of <i>The Folklore of Discworld</i>, a version of the Pied Pauper. Maurice, a cat, along with a number of rats has become intelligent to a point where they've learnt human spee</span>
  <span id="freeText731929832568852" style="display:none">This was one of the first <i>Discworld</i> novels I've ever read, the German translation back then though. I'm very pleased to report that the reading experience was even better this time - partly because the original is always better, partly because I now understood certain side-stabs and references, which was very rewarding.<br><br>It's part of <i>The Folklore of Discworld</i>, a version of the Pied Pauper. Maurice, a cat, along with a number of rats has become intelligent to a point where they've learnt human speech. Ever since then, Maurice has done his best to put the <u>rodents</u> (rat is considered a derogative term) to good work so <s>he</s> they can get rich. The trick is fairly simple, playing on human expectations - which is why their last coup doesn't work as they meet a human girl who practically lives fairytales. But that's a good thing, actually, as the town is in trouble and guess who can save everyone.<br><br>A very cute and funny look at reputations, stories, courage, having a conscience and the love of fairytales.<br><br>One of my favourite moments probably was towards the end when this song was sung (imagine it being sung to one of the usual military cadences):<br><i>"We fight dogs amd we chase cats ...<br>... ain't no trap can stop the rats!<br>Got no plague and got no fleas ...<br>... we drink poison, we steal cheese!<br>Mess with us and you shall see ...<br>... we'll put poison in your tea!<br>Here we fight and here we'll stay ...<br>... WE WILL NEVER GO AWAY!"</i><br>BWAHAHAHAHAHAHAHA!<br><br>And always remember: the best end to a conflict is when no side thinks they've lost - indeed!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1569863458i/28223628._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="731929832568852" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_759885569" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/759885569" />
    <a title="Rick Riordan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25375513-rick-riordan"><img alt="Rick Riordan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442449448p2/25375513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rick Riordan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rick Riordan" href="/user/show/25375513-rick-riordan">Rick Riordan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer759885569" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9404598370535547813">Another author I was slow in finding, Pratchett has a wicked and beautifully twisted sense of humor. I would call this book a recrafting of the Pied Piper story, but that really doesn't even begin to describe it. All the characters, human or otherwise, are wonderfully drawn, and the story is well worth your time. Sheesh, this guy is prolific, too. I need to get back to work now!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1891449218" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1891449218" />
    <a title="lucky little cat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38160628-lucky-little-cat"><img alt="lucky little cat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600336662p2/38160628.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1891449218?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="lucky little cat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="lucky little cat" href="/user/show/38160628-lucky-little-cat">lucky little cat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone who trusts my judgment, plus devotees of cuddly/ironic Muppet Show-caliber humor</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to lucky little cat by: </span>
      <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5253785-lyn" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Lyn</b>
</a>'s fab review reminded me to reread this one
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38160628-lucky-little-cat?shelf=hey-it-s-ya">hey-it-s-ya</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38160628-lucky-little-cat?shelf=books-b-might-like">books-b-might-like</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38160628-lucky-little-cat?shelf=young-adult-books-for-old-adults">young-adult-books-for-old-adults</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38160628-lucky-little-cat?shelf=it-s-funny">it-s-funny</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1891449218" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4651255717913338854">IF (like me) you've always been impatient with the Rincewind-heavy volumes of Sir Terry's <i>oeuvre,</i> you're in luck. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548068322ra/26949938.gif' width='450' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>Civilization begins with the tiniest steps</i><br/><br/><i>Maurice</i> is blessedly short on fart jokes* and long on Pratchett's brand of homespun philosophical irony. <br/><br/><i>Maurice</i> is a madly inventive retelling of <i>The Pied Piper,</i> featuring ragged-eared, fast-talking tomcat Maurice as the brains of the outfit. His cronies the rats can talk too, thanks to their hazardous-magical-waste diet amid the trash-heaps</span>
  <span id="freeText4651255717913338854" style="display:none">IF (like me) you've always been impatient with the Rincewind-heavy volumes of Sir Terry's <i>oeuvre,</i> you're in luck. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548068322ra/26949938.gif" width="450" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Civilization begins with the tiniest steps</i><br><br><i>Maurice</i> is blessedly short on fart jokes* and long on Pratchett's brand of homespun philosophical irony. <br><br><i>Maurice</i> is a madly inventive retelling of <i>The Pied Piper,</i> featuring ragged-eared, fast-talking tomcat Maurice as the brains of the outfit. His cronies the rats can talk too, thanks to their hazardous-magical-waste diet amid the trash-heaps behind Unseen University. <br><br>The book is funny, but more importantly, characters surprise us with their depth. Darktan, the toolbelt-swathed engineering-wizard rat, has a crisis of faith about his role as a leader. Other rats in his Clan are hammering out rules for ethical living, much to sharpster Maurice's disgust. <br><br>Even the dumb-looking piper kid is starting to give Maurice static about <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[scamming the populace with their fake plague of rats. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>One of my all-time favorite books along with Pratchett's <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/48002.Thief_of_Time__Discworld___26__Death___5_" title="Thief of Time (Discworld, #26; Death, #5) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Thief of Time</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2855034.Nation" title="Nation by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Nation</a>,</i> and his outstanding Tiffany Aching series beginning with<i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34494.The_Wee_Free_Men__Discworld___30__Tiffany_Aching___1_" title="The Wee Free Men (Discworld, #30; Tiffany Aching, #1) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wee Free Men</a>.</i><br><br>*not that there's anything <i>wrong</i> with fart jokes. But here, they're largely supplanted by tap-dancing rat gags à la vaudeville.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=2019">2019</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer11396344754332147128">This happened to be my first Pratchett book and why I did not love it, I still found myself greatly enjoying it whilst I read it. I do have this hunch where I think that absurdist fantasy(is that what you call it?) is probably not my thing. Whether I will like it more the more kind of these books I read or not, I’ll have to see but compared to what is considered as ‘normal’ fantasy, this is really far out there as many people have already noted. <br/><br/>It is full of talking rats and a cat and also some</span>
  <span id="freeText11396344754332147128" style="display:none">This happened to be my first Pratchett book and why I did not love it, I still found myself greatly enjoying it whilst I read it. I do have this hunch where I think that absurdist fantasy(is that what you call it?) is probably not my thing. Whether I will like it more the more kind of these books I read or not, I’ll have to see but compared to what is considered as ‘normal’ fantasy, this is really far out there as many people have already noted. <br /><br />It is full of talking rats and a cat and also some really random and dodgy implications of magic that certainly has me interested in reading more of his works. I do very much so like the fact that it is not at all like traditional fantasy with its swords, wizards and dark lords but breaks all of those boundaries and troops and writing something that is completely different. <br /><br />It does begin as a fairly lighthearted and humorous book, yet gets quite dark towards the end as the characters try to grapple towards the ending which I thought was handled in a decent manner. I have found out that this is apparently his first ‘YA’ Discworld book which I hope they his adult books are much better(though I have yet to read them as of the writing of this review, so really, I have no idea).<br /><br />I thought that this book was alright, I did not love it, nor hate it, but maybe again it may be because I’m not used to this kind of fantasy and going out of comfort zones takes maybe a few books to get used to that sort of take in the genre. 6/10</span>
  <a data-text-id="11396344754332147128" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText5955557215519073388" style="display:none"><b>Maurice watched them argue again. Humans, eh? Think they're lords of creation. Not like us cats. We <i>know</i> we are. Ever see a cat feed a human? Case proven.</b><br /><br />Maurice and his savvy, talking rodents arrive in town, ready once again to pull the old "Pied Piper" scheme. They scare the bejeezus out of the townsfolk, nibble on the comestibles and widdle everywhere. The citizens waste no time hiring Keith to play his magic flute, rats follow him out of the village, everybody splits the money and VOILA! - it's on to the next little hamlet.<br /><br />But Bad Blintz is different. This is a town that REALLY HATES RATS! There are full-time Rat Catchers paying 50 cents a tail and traps and poisons and a mysterious voice that gets inside your head and Malicia, a book-loving girl who won't stop talking.<br /><br />Will this be the end of the line for Maurice and his band of merry critters? <br /><br />This is a fairly cute tale with a good mix of adventure and humor. The rats (and their names, chosen from items found around the dump - Feedsfour, Nourishing, Big Savings and Dangerous Beans) - are the real stars of this show. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14304978950545281010">Re-read 2019<br/><br/>This may be billed as a YA novel by the redoubtable Pratchett, but I'm just going to shrug. It's fun and funny and I will always look at this novel as a sly reference to Vernor Vinge's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77711.A_Fire_Upon_the_Deep__Zones_of_Thought___1_' title='A Fire Upon the Deep (Zones of Thought, #1) by Vernor Vinge' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Fire Upon the Deep</a>, including multiple minds linked together to make a full intelligence.   <span id="freeText14304978950545281010" style="display:none">Re-read 2019<br /><br />This may be billed as a YA novel by the redoubtable Pratchett, but I'm just going to shrug. It's fun and funny and I will always look at this novel as a sly reference to Vernor Vinge's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77711.A_Fire_Upon_the_Deep__Zones_of_Thought___1_" title="A Fire Upon the Deep (Zones of Thought, #1) by Vernor Vinge" rel="nofollow noopener">A Fire Upon the Deep</a>, including multiple minds linked together to make a full intelligence. No, not wolves. RATS. Such a lovely image. <br /><br />But no, this isn't all this is. <br /><br />Talking rats and one very special talking cat and a stupid-looking boy con their way through Discworld. What more could anyone want? Villains, pied pipers, rats in human skin? Ah! But this is Pratchett and we've got all that and sausages that don't deserve the name sausage.<br /><br />It really is quite delightful. :)<br /><br />No. Not the sausage. The BOOK. :)</span>

<div id="review_77129859" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/77129859" />
    <a title="Mariel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/647547-mariel"><img alt="Mariel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451321467p2/647547.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/77129859?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mariel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mariel" href="/user/show/647547-mariel">Mariel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Crispin Glover</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Mariel by: </span>
      Michael Jackson
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer77129859" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8373548594066555698">What was up with that bullshit message of Ratatouille? (I hope I'm spelling that correctly. I'm gonna look so dumb! In my defense, I've always been the pickiest of eaters.) That whole "Don't steal from humans!" thing. They were rats! What did they care if humans stuck flags and paper umbrellas in every little thing? They shouldn't. The rat had as much right to saffron as stupid Lugini did.<br/><br/>The rodents in Terry Prachett's Maurice and his Educated Rodents are - D'oh! Sorry, Maurice! The AMAZING Mau</span>
  <span id="freeText8373548594066555698" style="display:none">What was up with that bullshit message of Ratatouille? (I hope I'm spelling that correctly. I'm gonna look so dumb! In my defense, I've always been the pickiest of eaters.) That whole "Don't steal from humans!" thing. They were rats! What did they care if humans stuck flags and paper umbrellas in every little thing? They shouldn't. The rat had as much right to saffron as stupid Lugini did.<br /><br />The rodents in Terry Prachett's Maurice and his Educated Rodents are - D'oh! Sorry, Maurice! The AMAZING Maurice and his Educated Rodents- anthropomorphized. But they are not slaves to the morality of man. They've got, as Richard Adams would say, dignity and animality all their own. They were seeking understanding of themselves and each other. I never cared much for definitions such as "allegory" or "fables". I care about "ring of truth" (if I think too much about types of stories I get confused and start labelling everything). Same goes for satire. Pratchett's satire would still be good if the things he was satirizing didn't exist. I wish all who wrote that would use that as their bench mark of success... Would it matter if you didn't know who it was? What they did? I don't really care that they are rats. Pratchett sure didn't. It was probably that that made their society and feeling of bonds (man, rat, whatever) feel... well, feel. No stupid Lugini tried to force rules on them.<br /><br />I'm not sure what was up with the less interesting kid people of the story. I KNOW Pratchett can do better than this. In fact, he can do amazing (see the Tiffany Aching series for pretty much the coolest little girl heroine from like ever). Enough about the stupid humans.<br /><br />I don't know if anyone reading this will relate to this or not. Sometimes I get this sensation when talking to people that they are constantly (this is exhausting) testing me to see if I'll stay interesting, or slip up and say something dumb (of course I'm going to do that). There's a kind of false barrier to that sort of "I'm saying this to see if you'll be shocked!" airs. Maurice could have had that. He does try so very hard. His gaze of the world and others is shrewd, somewhat hard out of necessity, playful too. It was a pleasure to read him come out of those expectations and into the necessity of honest interactions, in spite of himself (necessity if you don't want to be exhausted from constant expectations, anyway). They just wanted to make the most out of life. Who could blame them?<br /><br />The Pied Piper was one of my favorite fairy tales growing up. I'd feel sure that I wouldn't have been invited with the other kids to follow the music. Jesus, Mariel. (I liked the idea of everyone being gone way too much...)<br /><br />Anyone cannot cook. I can't. I smell a rat!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8373548594066555698" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1259302577" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1259302577" />
    <a title="Lindsay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10326608-lindsay"><img alt="Lindsay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588746288p2/10326608.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1259302577?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay" href="/user/show/10326608-lindsay">Lindsay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10326608-lindsay?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10326608-lindsay?shelf=humor">humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1259302577" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9422384839141541332">Part of the Pratchett reread with the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/162270-specfic-buddy-reads' rel='nofollow noopener'>SpecFic Buddy Reads</a> group in 2019.<br/><br/>Maurice is an intelligent talking cat that has masterminded a scheme where his gang of intelligent talking rats and a human boy go from town-to-town implementing a plague of rats and then having the boy pipe them out of town for a fee. The group arrive at the town of Bad Blintz for one last job only to find a town that already has a rat problem. A very odd one.<br/><br/>This is only my second read of this story since soon after its pu</span>
  <span id="freeText9422384839141541332" style="display:none">Part of the Pratchett reread with the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/162270-specfic-buddy-reads" rel="nofollow noopener">SpecFic Buddy Reads</a> group in 2019.<br /><br />Maurice is an intelligent talking cat that has masterminded a scheme where his gang of intelligent talking rats and a human boy go from town-to-town implementing a plague of rats and then having the boy pipe them out of town for a fee. The group arrive at the town of Bad Blintz for one last job only to find a town that already has a rat problem. A very odd one.<br /><br />This is only my second read of this story since soon after its publication, and I had considered it a lesser work from the author. Not since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34506.The_Light_Fantastic__Discworld___2__Rincewind__2_" title="The Light Fantastic (Discworld, #2; Rincewind #2) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Light Fantastic</a> has a reread changed my opinion of a Discworld book more. I loved everything about these books, from the power of leadership, to the idea of a philosopher rat going ahead of his fellows to disarm ideas like other rats would disarm traps, to the boy Keith and his absolute acceptance that the talking rats and cat are just a different sort of people. Even the idea of a rat utopia that is floated at the start of the book is examined and rejected for a much better reality.<br /><br />Even more powerfully, and timely in 2019, is the rejection of authoritarianism that doesn't care about individuals or negotiation.<br /><br />A hidden gem of the series IMO.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9422384839141541332" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1286483394" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6212301743411744296">This is Terry Pratchett's first YA Discworld novel and as to be expected it is a lot of fun.It's based on the Pied Piper story with Maurice the talking cat, a band of talking rats (they all ate something strange at the dump) and a stupid looking kid who plays the flute. They go from village to village scamming the villagers into paying for the piper to rid the town of rats who are running amok, widdling on the cheese and swimming in the cream. The rats are very cute with names they've taking fro</span>
  <span id="freeText6212301743411744296" style="display:none">This is Terry Pratchett's first YA Discworld novel and as to be expected it is a lot of fun.It's based on the Pied Piper story with Maurice the talking cat, a band of talking rats (they all ate something strange at the dump) and a stupid looking kid who plays the flute. They go from village to village scamming the villagers into paying for the piper to rid the town of rats who are running amok, widdling on the cheese and swimming in the cream. The rats are very cute with names they've taking from supermarket items such as Nourishing, Hamnpork, Peaches and Dangerous Beans. Some are trap disposal experts and some are champion widdlers sent out to cause maximum distress to housewives. <br /><br />This story starts with the troop arriving at a strange village where nary a rat is seen and two resident rat catchers are up to something very bad....</span>

<div id="review_51608167" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/51608167" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597876967p2/1343864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/51608167?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=orphalins">orphalins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=ridiculously-prolific-authors">ridiculously-prolific-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=swashbucklers-capers-and-heists">swashbucklers-capers-and-heists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=kid-lit">kid-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=books-i-missed-during-childhood">books-i-missed-during-childhood</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=award-winners">award-winners</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=anglophilia">anglophilia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer51608167" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8441120952919980923">I very much enjoyed Terry Pratchett’s first foray into young adult literature. I know he’s written a handful of YA books (many of them also set in the Discworld), but I wish he had written more. He was very good at it!<br/><br/>One thing I loved as a kid, and which I still love now, is when children’s books have darker edges to them. Kids live in this world same as adults. They worry about death and violence and hunger. Like, kids are people, too, and their literature shouldn’t ignore or sugarcoat those a</span>
  <span id="freeText8441120952919980923" style="display:none">I very much enjoyed Terry Pratchett’s first foray into young adult literature. I know he’s written a handful of YA books (many of them also set in the Discworld), but I wish he had written more. He was very good at it!<br /><br />One thing I loved as a kid, and which I still love now, is when children’s books have darker edges to them. Kids live in this world same as adults. They worry about death and violence and hunger. Like, kids are people, too, and their literature shouldn’t ignore or sugarcoat those aspects of humanity. The best kids and young adult books are always the ones that know this. I guessed going in Pratchett would be that kind of author, and I was right.<br /><br />The Amazing Maurice is a cat, a cat who can talk. His companions are rats, rats who can talk. And think. (It all has to do with a pile of magical refuse they all ate out of at the back of Unseen University in Ankh-Morpork, long story.) What they have chosen to do with their sapience is to befriend a lonely young boy and use him to perpetuate a scam on a bunch of villages, where all the rats invade a town and do rat things (pee on stuff, eat it, etc.) until the village decides to employ the services of a piper who is conveniently in town, at which point all the rats will magically fade away. (This is a twisted take on the Pied Piper tale.)<br /><br />But when they get to a town that already has a rat problem, and things there are very strange, their scheme takes a turn.<br /><br />The best part about this book, aside from criminal talking animals, is the existential crisis all the rats are going through. They all have names like Dangerous Beans and Hamnpork and Sardines, but some rats are smarter and more enlightened than others. So there’s this whole thing about rats learning what it means to be people and not rats that was as moving as it was ridiculous. It also works really well as a contrast against the “villain” of the book, a rat king, which was disgusting, don’t google it it’s a real thing.<br /><br />Even if you haven’t read any other Discworld books, this is worth checking out, especially if you have young readers looking for some reading that’s smart and a bit cheeky.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8441120952919980923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1884405002" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15665528082576741655">Talk to the paw, because the whiskers aren't listening. Overdrive has informed me that I listened to the entirety of this. I say, it's debatable.<br/><br/>Here's why Pratchett is a miss with me. I want to experience the story as a character. This requires a deep point of view. But Pratchett always does this (to the tune of Row Your Boat):<br/><br/><i>Tell, tell, tell, the tale,<br/>tell the fricking tale.<br/>If you want to be shown,<br/>you can go to Hale.</i><br/><br/>Yes, one minute you are a star whistling through the cosmos, the next, a cat </span>
  <span id="freeText15665528082576741655" style="display:none">Talk to the paw, because the whiskers aren't listening. Overdrive has informed me that I listened to the entirety of this. I say, it's debatable.<br /><br />Here's why Pratchett is a miss with me. I want to experience the story as a character. This requires a deep point of view. But Pratchett always does this (to the tune of Row Your Boat):<br /><br /><i>Tell, tell, tell, the tale,<br />tell the fricking tale.<br />If you want to be shown,<br />you can go to Hale.</i><br /><br />Yes, one minute you are a star whistling through the cosmos, the next, a cat in the alley. It's just how Grandpa Terry rolls. He also uses modern slang in a medieval setting, which pulls me right out. Not to mention a cast of a thousand fools, every frickin' time.<br /><br />Instead of a main character who will do anything to achieve a goal, we usually have a lunkhead who rolls around in the mud until something happens. Maybe this is better read, but I'd avoid the audio book.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18418827077274242702">I have read this book at least 15 times, I swear! Or even more. It is officially the number one book I have read the most out of every book I have read. Which is amazing, because when I got it, I didn't even expect for me to like it that much. Surprise, surprise.   <span id="freeText18418827077274242702" style="display:none">I have read this book at least 15 times, I swear! Or even more. It is officially the number one book I have read the most out of every book I have read. Which is amazing, because when I got it, I didn't even expect for me to like it that much. Surprise, surprise. I loved it. <br /><br />My favorite characters were, Amazing Maurice, Peaches, stupid looking kid/Keith, Darktan, Dangerous Beans, and Sardines. <br /><br />And the plot. It was an amazing retelling. One of the best. I also don't really like the Pied Piper story, but this was amazing. <br /><br />I HAVE READ THIS BOOK SO MANY TIMES THAT I CAN LITERALLY QUOTE SCENES! Yes, I love it that much. And yes, I have read it that many times. YAH!<br /><br />I would recommend this book to kids ages 9 and up. I really wish I had a hardcover version that is not a mass market paperback, but at the moment, I don't think I will.</span>

<div id="review_2093740" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2093740" />
    <a title="Alice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/120713-alice"><img alt="Alice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1181244112p2/120713.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2093740?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alice" href="/user/show/120713-alice">Alice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2093740" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9378605784283789236">Well, I have definitely learned a lot about rats. I have mixed feelings about this book. Terry Pratchett is usually SO GOOD at mixing light-hearted silliness with a more macabre subject matter, but this time something felt a little… off. The rats are great at first, a nice blend of ratty grossness and the angst that comes with sudden enlightenment… or puberty. The rat characters are well-developed and as authentic as a bunch of talking rats can be. Maurice the cat is also a wonderful character.<br/><br/>B</span>
  <span id="freeText9378605784283789236" style="display:none">Well, I have definitely learned a lot about rats. I have mixed feelings about this book. Terry Pratchett is usually SO GOOD at mixing light-hearted silliness with a more macabre subject matter, but this time something felt a little… off. The rats are great at first, a nice blend of ratty grossness and the angst that comes with sudden enlightenment… or puberty. The rat characters are well-developed and as authentic as a bunch of talking rats can be. Maurice the cat is also a wonderful character.<br /><br />But something is not quite right towards the middle. I think things went all pear-shaped with the introduction of the disembodied voice that turns out to be a Rat King, a phenomenon I would have much preferred to remain ignorant of. The whole rat-king business doesn’t seem to quite fit, or maybe I’m just to squeamish to handle the idea of a bunch of live rats with their tails fused together. Ew. In any case, the disembodied voice business just didn’t jive with me and felt out of place in this story.<br /><br />Also, I got fuddled with this book in the middle section, trying to figure out whether it’s really meant to be a children’s story or a weird children’s-story-for-adults thing. There are some very very oblique sexual references having to do with the more enlightened rats, and some other things that threw me off. Perhaps it’s that the rats are not quite “Mr. Bunnsy” enough for children- they walk and talk like story-book creatures, but they still pee on everything and eat each other and commit little ratty murders. And that’s troublesome. It’s also troublesome that the rats talk about philosophy, clearly not something we want children exposed to. I guess the easy-reading laugh-a-minute feel of most of the discworld books got diluted somehow in this one. <br /><br />Despite how hinky the middle section is, the ending is really quite satisfying, at least to me. I suppose a law student would a contract to be a good narrative resolution. It feels more authentic than the middle bits and pokes a bit of fun at authority, tourism and government, so all’s well that ends well.<br /><br />Here’s my advice- go read everything Terry Pratchett has ever written, starting with Good Omens and then blasting through Discworld like it’s your job. Read A Hat Full of Sky and the Wee Free Men, which are also geared for a younger audience. Throw this book on the end of the list and see how it goes. And, for the sake of everything good and decent in the world do NOT do a Google search for “Rat King.” Just don’t. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9378605784283789236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11433866277219040487" style="display:none">Was the Pied Piper a true story?<br /><br />Poor Cinder- oops I mean Malicia...<br />‘I expect you’re very keen to know all about me,’ said Malicia. ‘I expect you’re just too polite to ask.’<br /><br />‘Gosh, yes,’ said Maurice.<br /><br />‘Well, you probably won’t be surprised to know that I’ve got two dreadful step-sisters,’ said Malicia. ‘And I have to do all the chores!’<br /><br />‘Gosh, really,’ said Maurice, wondering if there were any more fish-heads and, if there were any more fish-heads, whether they were worth all this.<br /><br />‘Well, most of the chores,’ said Malicia, as if revealing an unfortunate fact. ‘Some of them, definitely. I have to clean up my own room, you know! And it’s extremely untidy!’<br /><br />‘Gosh, really.’<br /><br />‘And it’s very nearly the smallest bedroom. There are practically no cupboards and I’m running out of bookshelf space!’<br /><br />With tip of the hat to "The Famous Five"...<br />‘My father shouted a lot and sent for Blunkett and Spears, too,’ said Malicia. ‘They’re the rat-catchers! And you know what that means, don’t you?’<br /><br />Maurice and Keith looked at one another. ‘Let’s pretend we don’t,’ said Maurice.<br /><br />‘It means we can break into their shed and solve the mystery of the bootlace tails!’ said Malicia. She gave Maurice a critical look. ‘Of course, it would be more … satisfying if we were four children and a dog, which is the right number for an adventure, but we’ll make do with what we’ve got.’<br /><br />The secret passage cliche...<br />Malicia leaned against the wall with incredible nonchalance. There was not a click. A panel in the floor did not slide back. <br /><br />‘Probably the wrong place,’ she said. ‘I’ll just rest my arm innocently on this coat hook.’ A sudden door in the wall completely failed to happen. <br /><br />‘Of course, it’d help if there was an ornate candlestick,’ said Malicia. ‘They’re always a sure-fire secret passage lever. Every adventurer knows that.’<br /><br />And more...<br />‘Ye-es,’ she said. ‘That usually works, in stories. It’s often the stupid person who comes up with the good idea by accident.’ <br />She crouched down and peered into the hole. ‘There’s a sort of little lever,’ she said. ‘I’ll just give it a little push …’<br /><br />There was a clonk under the floor, part of it swung back, and Keith dropped out of sight.<br /><br />‘Oh, yes,’ said Malicia. ‘I thought something like that would probably happen …’<br /><br />More Fairy tales...<br />‘My granny and my great-aunt were very famous story-tellers, you know,’ said Malicia eventually, in a strained little voice. ‘Agoniza and Eviscera Grim.’<br /><br />‘You said,’ said Keith.<br /><br />‘My mother would have been a good story-teller, too, but my father doesn’t like stories. That’s why I’ve changed my name to Grim for professional purposes.’<br /><br />‘Really …’<br /><br />‘I used to get beaten when I was small for telling stories,’ Malicia went on.<br /><br />‘Beaten?’ said Keith.<br /><br />‘All right, then, smacked,’ said Malicia. ‘On the leg. But it did hurt. My father says you can’t run a city on stories. He says you have to be practical.’<br /><br />Cats:Lords of Creation...<br />Maurice watched them argue again. Humans, eh? Think they’re lords of creation. Not like us cats. We know we are. Ever see a cat feed a human? Case proven.<br /><br />Alien crop circles...<br />It’s just like crop circles. No matter how many aliens own up to making them, there are always a few diehards who believe that humans go out with garden rollers in the middle of the night—’<br /><br />Recent adventures...<br />Remember last month? <br />When she tracked down the Mysterious Headless Horseman?’<br /><br />‘Well, you must admit he was a horseman, sir.’<br /><br />‘That is true. But he was also a short man with a very high collar. And he was the chief tax-gatherer from Mintz. I’m still getting official letters about it! Tax-gatherers do not as a rule like young ladies dropping on them out of trees!<br /><br />...and more adventures...<br />‘The Mystery of Smuggler’s Windmill, sir,’ said the sergeant, rolling his eyes.<br /><br />‘Which turned out to be Mr Vogel the town clerk and Mrs Schuman the shoemaker’s wife, who happened to be there merely because of their shared interest in studying the habits of barn owls …’<br /><br />‘… and Mr Vogel had his trousers off because he’d torn them on a nail …’ said the sergeant, not looking at the mayor.<br /><br />‘… which Mrs Schuman was very kindly repairing for him,’ said the mayor.<br /><br />‘By moonlight,’ said the sergeant.<br /><br />‘She happens to have very good eyesight!’ snapped the mayor. ‘And she didn’t deserve to be bound and gagged along with Mr Vogel, who caught quite a chill as a result!<br /><br />The (almost) end of the rats...<br />And that was almost the end of the story.How the crowd yelled when rats erupted from every hole and drain. How they cheered when both pipers danced out of the town, with the rats racing along behind them. How they whistled when the rats plunged off the bridge into the river.<br /><br />They didn’t notice that some rats stayed on the bridge, urging the others with shouts of ‘Remember, strong regular strokes!’ and ‘There’s a nice beach just downstream!’ and ‘Hit the water feet first, it won’t hurt so much!’<br /><br />Even if they had noticed, they probably wouldn’t have said anything. Details like that don’t fit in.<br /><br />And the piper danced off over the hills and never, ever came back.<br /><br /><br />Enjoy!<br /></span>

<div id="review_1937134222" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1937134222" />
    <a title="YouKneeK" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek"><img alt="YouKneeK" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386369592p2/25923230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1937134222?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="YouKneeK" class="user" itemprop="url" name="YouKneeK" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek">YouKneeK</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6441351-the-amazing-maurice-and-his-educated-rodents">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=completed-series">completed-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1937134222" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4895763586703450004"><i>The Amazing Maurice and His Educated Rodents</i> is the first young adult <i>Discworld</i> book. It was a short book, and a cute story, but I thought it was pretty substantial in terms of both plot and messages. The plot was certainly more substantial than many of his adult <i>Discworld</i> books. I didn’t think there was quite as much humor, but it had its funny moments.<br/><br/>The basic premise is that some of the rats in Ankh-Morpork, after eating magical rubbish dumped by the residents of the Unseen University, have </span>
  <span id="freeText4895763586703450004" style="display:none"><i>The Amazing Maurice and His Educated Rodents</i> is the first young adult <i>Discworld</i> book. It was a short book, and a cute story, but I thought it was pretty substantial in terms of both plot and messages. The plot was certainly more substantial than many of his adult <i>Discworld</i> books. I didn’t think there was quite as much humor, but it had its funny moments.<br /><br />The basic premise is that some of the rats in Ankh-Morpork, after eating magical rubbish dumped by the residents of the Unseen University, have become intelligent. They can talk in human speech, read, and think rationally. Maurice, a cat, has gained similar abilities. Maurice is, like most cats, opportunistic. He finds himself a “stupid-looking kid” who can play a pipe, and starts up a scam with the rats and the kid in which they all travel to various towns, the rats freak out the residents, and the stupid-looking kid plays the pipe and pretends he’s charming the rats into leaving the town. For a fee, of course. The story begins as they approach a new town where they plan to execute their scam. Things don’t go as planned.<br /> <br />I enjoyed the story pretty well. It had some fun characters, both of the human and non-human variety. I particularly liked Maurice, of course! Even though this may seem like a weird comparison to anybody who has read both books, I kept having flashbacks to <i>Watership Down</i>. The books are very different in most ways, but there were some similarities in tone and even a couple similar events. If I hadn’t read <i>Watership Down</i> so recently, I doubt I would have had the same reaction.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4895763586703450004" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3141416354" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3141416354" />
    <a title="K.A. Ashcomb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/81350561-k-a-ashcomb"><img alt="K.A. Ashcomb" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534101017p2/81350561.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3141416354?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K.A. Ashcomb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K.A. Ashcomb" href="/user/show/81350561-k-a-ashcomb">K.A. Ashcomb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552552028" href="/book/show/64333.The_Amazing_Maurice_and_His_Educated_Rodents">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3141416354" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5321401957603274721">How should I describe this book? It is a lovely story about speaking animals with a darker spin and serious tone, yet, light and funny. Now go and read it. That is all you need to know. To those who are fans of Discworld novels, this is definitely a Discworld book. There is no doubt about it.<br/><br/>But read on if you want to hear my thoughts. Terry Pratchett has outdone himself with this book. He has gotten the mood just right. As I wrote before, it is fun and light, yet, dark and serious. But you can </span>
  <span id="freeText5321401957603274721" style="display:none">How should I describe this book? It is a lovely story about speaking animals with a darker spin and serious tone, yet, light and funny. Now go and read it. That is all you need to know. To those who are fans of Discworld novels, this is definitely a Discworld book. There is no doubt about it.<br /><br />But read on if you want to hear my thoughts. Terry Pratchett has outdone himself with this book. He has gotten the mood just right. As I wrote before, it is fun and light, yet, dark and serious. But you can easily ignore the last two and enjoy the well-written story of personal growth. Growth of both the Amazing Maurice, the rats, and their relationship to the humans. The only one who is not changing at all is the weird-looking kid, but that is okay, he is already who he should be, and the reader gets to know him better as the story progress.<br /><br />The book has everything for everyone. A hint of love. A whole lot of adventure and courage. To those who like to ponder more profound things about the nature of humans and rats and how we all are entangled in this world, is like a treasure map, nuggets hidden here and there. It shows how cruel humans are and can be, that dark tone you might have been looking for. It moralizes a bit if that is something you don't like, but I'm one who comes from a generation of those who enjoy moral stories in their work of fiction, especially if such a conviction is well-argued.<br /><br />About the content: Darktan's (rat) battle speeches and the conflict of leadership with Hamnpork and how it plays out is such a beauty. Dangerous Beans' visions for the rat clan are good contemplation about how civilizations should be organized and how we relate to each other. How the other rats react, is just right. That is how we act, but luckily not all the time. Sometimes rebellious thoughts get in and there is change. All those points Pratchett brings to life with his side notes, which made me have that soft smile on my face and a giddy feeling inside even when he is talking about cannibalism, lying, stealing, questioning who should rule, asking who deserves and what, who has a consciousness and who hasn't, who to eat and who not. But he wrote it all in so well that this is still a children's book and you can read it without the fear of contamination.<br /><br />My only complaint is how he handles I and you question of animals. There has been a lot of studies done that animals have a concept of self-hood, the mirror test and other complex ones. The idea that human speech brought the concept of I to the rats and Maurice is too restricting. But luckily the book doesn't leave it there. Pratchett writes about the keekees (the normal rats) and how they should be treated and Dangerous Beans makes a point through the book called Mr. Bunnsy Has an Adventure that all rats are important and are due respect. The whole concept of speech and what it did to the rats and Maurice will get more interesting towards the end, but no spoilers. Sorry about getting excited. This book is so good for both adults and young, thinking of buying this for my nephew as a birthday present.<br /><br />Thank you for reading and have a ratty day!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5321401957603274721" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12368331056565103192">A children's take on Discworld - but while that may mean it's simpler, it doesn't mean it's not just as dark. Not ideal for very young children, those prone to nightmares, or those who don't like rats...<br/><br/>For adult fans, it's a pleasant return to some elements of Pratchett's earlier writing (particularly the Bromeliad), with all the polish and sophistication of his later work. Doesn't read as any more child-oriented than many of his early Discworld novels, like <i>Equal Rites</i> or <i>Mort</i> - less sly sexua</span>
  <span id="freeText12368331056565103192" style="display:none">A children's take on Discworld - but while that may mean it's simpler, it doesn't mean it's not just as dark. Not ideal for very young children, those prone to nightmares, or those who don't like rats...<br /><br />For adult fans, it's a pleasant return to some elements of Pratchett's earlier writing (particularly the Bromeliad), with all the polish and sophistication of his later work. Doesn't read as any more child-oriented than many of his early Discworld novels, like <i>Equal Rites</i> or <i>Mort</i> - less sly sexual innuendo, more threat of characters being eaten alive by rats, you kind of takes your choice... anyway, it's still enjoyable for adults, but I can see why marketers might think it would work better with younger readers. Irritating, precocious children are probably the target audience here...<br /><br />Anyway, a proper but still rather short review <a href="https://vacuouswastrel.wordpress.com/2015/07/18/the-amazing-maurice-and-his-educated-rodents-by-terry-pratchett/" rel="nofollow noopener">up on my blog</a> (if the darn link works this time...)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4902618696397727673">I feared once again that this would be another Pratchett book I'll have to give less than 5 stars. Alas, I was wrong and boy, am I glad. The first 2/5 was a little boring, or maybe it was so because I had to read it in really small chunks because I was travelling a lot over the past three days. But then, it got great. It got deep, complicated, with an unexpected plot twist, and once again Sir Terry taught us that both the greatest sin and beauty of man is humanity. Because, as usual, it was huma</span>
  <span id="freeText4902618696397727673" style="display:none">I feared once again that this would be another Pratchett book I'll have to give less than 5 stars. Alas, I was wrong and boy, am I glad. The first 2/5 was a little boring, or maybe it was so because I had to read it in really small chunks because I was travelling a lot over the past three days. But then, it got great. It got deep, complicated, with an unexpected plot twist, and once again Sir Terry taught us that both the greatest sin and beauty of man is humanity. Because, as usual, it was humans who couldn't get it right, and cats and rats who definitely could and did. And at the end of the day, it's only important that someone gets it right and fixes the mess, even if they're small and shouldn't be able to talk.</span>
