<div id="review_3606161852" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3606161852" />

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3606161852?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Campbell" href="/user/show/72416163-michael-campbell">Michael Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3606161852" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11624364333818664082">No one writes an animal character quite like Terry Pratchett. Not only did he understand humanity as well as anyone, but he understands rats, cats, and dogs just as well, apparently. The amount of depth and development given characters with names like Dangerous Beans and Darktan is astounding. I sympathized more with the rat characters than I have most human characters.<br/><br/>It was a fun story with a dark edge, and it was a nice social commentary. I question it being a children's book and would call i</span>
  <span id="freeText11624364333818664082" style="display:none">No one writes an animal character quite like Terry Pratchett. Not only did he understand humanity as well as anyone, but he understands rats, cats, and dogs just as well, apparently. The amount of depth and development given characters with names like Dangerous Beans and Darktan is astounding. I sympathized more with the rat characters than I have most human characters.<br /><br />It was a fun story with a dark edge, and it was a nice social commentary. I question it being a children's book and would call it middle grade fiction. <br /><br />The cat was my favorite, but I knew that would happen from the onset. Plenty of wit, a good deal of wisdom, and characters that reach out and grab you. It's a Terry Pratchett book through and through, and that's all that really needs to be said for it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11624364333818664082" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780060012359" href="/book/show/61653.The_Amazing_Maurice_and_His_Educated_Rodents">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3236721-cory-hughart?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3236721-cory-hughart?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3236721-cory-hughart?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3236721-cory-hughart?shelf=british">british</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3236721-cory-hughart?shelf=pratchett">pratchett</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer127398992" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17530631653983817162">This is a 'young adult' novel? I think Terry must have gotten fed up with the run-of-the-mill children's books and decided to do a sort of parody of them, one where the characters constantly make references to the fact that real life is not like 'Mr. Bunnsy Has an Adventure'.<br/><br/>This is definitely a novel that teens can digest, but there are some parts that are even more grim and depressing than many of Pratchett's 'adult' books. I am reading the Discworld series in order of publication, and I was d</span>
  <span id="freeText17530631653983817162" style="display:none">This is a 'young adult' novel? I think Terry must have gotten fed up with the run-of-the-mill children's books and decided to do a sort of parody of them, one where the characters constantly make references to the fact that real life is not like 'Mr. Bunnsy Has an Adventure'.<br /><br />This is definitely a novel that teens can digest, but there are some parts that are even more grim and depressing than many of Pratchett's 'adult' books. I am reading the Discworld series in order of publication, and I was dreading having to get through a 'young adult' novel to be complete, but this didn't break my momentum in the least. If you are reading them in order as well, you'll love this one too.</span>

Case proven."<br/><br/>"'If you don't turn your life into a story, you just become a part of someone else's story.' <br/>'And what if your story doesn't work?' <br/>'You keep changing it until you find one that does.'"</span>

<div id="review_168812933" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/168812933" />
    <a title="Toby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5454475-toby"><img alt="Toby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542247337p2/5454475.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/168812933?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Toby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Toby" href="/user/show/5454475-toby">Toby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552546935" href="/book/show/1191652.The_Amazing_Maurice_His_Educated_Rodents">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5454475-toby?shelf=fantastical">fantastical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5454475-toby?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168812933" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3097775054725775471">Been looking forward to this one, the first YA Discworld novel, and probably the best despite not offering the publisher's the chance to print money by turning in to a standalone YA series - that would come later of course. By riffing on the Pied Piper legend/fairy tale Pratchett is playing it safe, using the readers prior knowledge to introduce his own sense of playful storytelling and humour, as well as allowing himself to softly broach his pet subjects of fate vs free will, self-determination</span>
  <span id="freeText3097775054725775471" style="display:none">Been looking forward to this one, the first YA Discworld novel, and probably the best despite not offering the publisher's the chance to print money by turning in to a standalone YA series - that would come later of course. By riffing on the Pied Piper legend/fairy tale Pratchett is playing it safe, using the readers prior knowledge to introduce his own sense of playful storytelling and humour, as well as allowing himself to softly broach his pet subjects of fate vs free will, self-determination, communism vs capitalism, the comfort and absurdity of religion and the foibles of humanity in general. And it works really well thanks to his fun "educated rodents" and the character arc of the arrogant overseer, the Amazing Maurice. Pretty classic Discworld, even if the edges are softened or a younger audience.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3097775054725775471" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('M9h4ApcRFZ2/+ydjguvXgIknFroLBhMPAGjZVHa+NN8J/hHQLE/c9RjQkwJ1Ht1fX3jxcsWLnWhbFp/lu/3GRQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MzNrUlTBNrZXsoi1dFB4HFBrQzJJKr3c0kYSA4GQPaYJFQKA75//3vCZPNSDpXLDhjSk+oenM7uJOFSyTNPPPA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett">About Terry Pratchett</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1235562205p3/1654.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett">Terry Pratchett
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
35,100
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5946363431507255663">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br/><br/>Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, i</span>
  <span id="freeText5946363431507255663" style="display:none">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br /><br />Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, including his first Discworld novel, <i>The Color of Magic</i>, in 1983. In 1987, he turned to writing full time. <br /><br />There are over 40 books in the Discworld series, of which four are written for children. The first of these, <i>The Amazing Maurice and His Educated Rodents</i>, won the Carnegie Medal. <br /><br />A non-Discworld book, <i>Good Omens</i>, his 1990 collaboration with Neil Gaiman, has been a longtime bestseller and was reissued in hardcover by William Morrow in early 2006 (it is also available as a mass market paperback - Harper Torch, 2006 - and trade paperback - Harper Paperbacks, 2006). <br /><br />In 2008, Harper Children's published Terry's standalone non-Discworld YA novel, <i>Nation</i>. Terry published <i>Snuff</i> in October 2011. <br /><br />Regarded as one of the most significant contemporary English-language satirists, Pratchett has won numerous literary awards, was named an Officer of the British Empire (OBE) “for services to literature” in 1998, and has received honorary doctorates from the University of Warwick in 1999, the University of Portsmouth in 2001, the University of Bath in 2003, the University of Bristol in 2004, Buckinghamshire New University in 2008, the University of Dublin in 2008, Bradford University in 2009, the University of Winchester in 2009, and The Open University in 2013 for his contribution to Public Service.<br /><br />In Dec. of 2007, Pratchett disclosed that he had been diagnosed with Alzheimer's disease. On 18 Feb, 2009, he was knighted by Queen Elizabeth II.<br /><br />He was awarded the World Fantasy Life Achievement Award in 2010.<br /><br />Sir Terry Pratchett passed away on 12th March 2015.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5946363431507255663" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

        $('bookCover_64218').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
